every other block.\n\n## Why a gateway now (CAMPAIGN.md D1)\n\nThe Pantheon-API transport swap is deferred to post-campaign, but the **seam** is built now so\nthat swap is a one-module change instead of a scattered edit. Consolidating the eleven wrappers\ninto one importable, typed, gated module is that seam, and is the first real logic move of the\ncampaign (LEDGER.md I0 open-question for I2).\n\n## Move mechanics\n\n### The import-back strategy (keeps the remnant working, one seam for tests)\n\n`psh/gateway.py` holds the eleven defs **verbatim** (bodies unchanged; only the return-type\nannotations change, below). `psh/_legacy.py` re-imports them so its ~54 existing call sites and\nthe `sc`-exposure block keep resolving unchanged:\n\n```python\n# psh/_legacy.py, replacing the removed defs:\nfrom psh.gateway import (\n    GatewayResult,\n    TerminusError,\n    drush,\n    drush_error,\n    drush_php_script,\n    fix_drush_output,\n    run_terminus,\n    terminus,\n    terminus_data,\n    wp,\n    wp_error,\n    wp_eval,\n)\n```\n\nConsequences, all verified:\n\n- `psh._legacy.terminus` / `psh._legacy.run_terminus` / `psh._legacy.TerminusError` /\n  `psh._legacy.GatewayResult` etc. still exist (bound to the gateway objects), so `psh.<name>`\n  through the test `psh` fixture keeps resolving. `sc.terminus = terminus` (`_legacy` line 1643)\n  still assigns the gateway function, so `reset_sc.terminus is psh.terminus` stays true\n  (`test_terminus_contract.py::test_check_helpers_are_exposed_on_sc`).\n- **No `_legacy` imports are orphaned by the move.** Every import the moved code used has other\n  live users in `_legacy`: `html` (plugin/module notice bodies, ~9 sites), `time` (`time.sleep`\n  at db-retry line 1373), `escape` (50 call sites), `Any` (`process_config`), `subprocess`\n  (PHP inliner), `json`/`re`/`NamedTuple`. Verified by grep; the implementer re-verifies and\n  removes only what its change actually orphans (there should be none).\n\n### `GatewayResult` (CAMPAIGN.md §6)\n\n```python\nclass GatewayResult(NamedTuple):\n    result: Any\n    errors: str\n    fatal: bool\n```\n\nApplied as the return annotation and constructed at each return of the 3-tuple wrappers:\n`run_terminus`, `terminus`, `wp`, `wp_eval`, `drush`, `drush_php_script`. `fix_drush_output`\nkeeps its 2-tuple, annotated `-> tuple[str, str]`. `terminus_data` returns just the result,\nannotated `-> Any`. `wp_error`/`drush_error` return `-> list[dict[str, str]]`. This discharges\nCAMPAIGN.md §6's house-style-tuple-hint replacement for every moved def in one pass (D2 — cleaned\nas it moves, never fixed in place in the remnant).\n\n`GatewayResult` is a `tuple` subclass, so every positional unpack (`result, errors, fatal = …`)\nand every `== (a, b, c)` comparison in call sites and tests is unchanged — behavior-preserving,\nno golden impact (the return type is invisible to rendered output). The first element of\n`run_terminus`/`wp_eval` is textual output; the generic field name `result` covers it and no\ncaller reads the fields by name, so this is a naming nicety only.\n\n`GatewayResult` is **not** added to `sc`: no `check`/`plugin` consumer references the type name\n(they unpack positionally), so adding it would be dead façade surface (CAMPAIGN.md §17 Q4).\n\n### Column-0 literal invariant (Invariant 8)\n\n`wp_error` and `drush_error` each contain a multi-line `f\"\"\"...\"\"\"` whose continuation lines\nbegin at **column 0**. They are module-level defs today and stay module-level defs in\n`gateway.py` — identical nesting, so the interior bytes are unchanged. The implementer MUST move\nthese literals **verbatim** and MUST NOT re-indent them; `git diff -w` is not acceptable evidence\n(CAMPAIGN.md Invariant 8). Evidence required in the task report: the four e2e goldens\nbyte-identical (they are the tripwire), plus a token-level or `diff`-of-extracted-literal check\non the two blocks.\n\n## Seams (declared before implementation — CAMPAIGN.md §Spec quality bar)\n\nThe canonical in-process seam for anything routed through the wrappers becomes\n**`psh.gateway.run_terminus`**. Reason: after the move, `terminus`/`wp`/`drush` resolve\n`run_terminus` in the **gateway** module's namespace, not `_legacy`'s. Patching\n`psh._legacy.run_terminus` (i.e. `setattr(psh, \"run_terminus\", …)`) would rebind only the\nremnant's name and the wrappers would call the real subprocess — a silent test defect (PD#14).\n\nA conftest fixture provides the handle:\n\n```python\n@pytest.fixture\ndef gateway(psh):\n    \"\"\"The psh.gateway module (psh._legacy has already imported it).\"\"\"\n    import psh.gateway\n    return psh.gateway\n```\n\n**What must repoint (function-attribute patches):** only the four files whose tests patch\n`run_terminus` **and then call a wrapper** — the patch target changes from `psh` to `gateway`:\n\n| File | Lines patching `run_terminus` |\n|---|---|\n| `tests/integration/test_terminus_contract.py` | 21, 29, 38, 44, 49, 57, 67, 82 |\n| `tests/integration/test_wrappers.py` | 23, 31, 38, 46, 54, 62 |\n| `tests/integration/test_terminus_seam.py` | 15, 26 |\n| `tests/integration/test_regressions.py` | 31, 48 |\n\n**What must NOT repoint (module-singleton patches — verified they keep working):**\n\n- `setattr(psh.time, \"sleep\", …)` and `setattr(psh.subprocess, \"Popen\", …)` mutate the shared\n  `time` / `subprocess` **module** objects, which gateway and `_legacy` both `import`. Gateway's\n  `time.sleep(5)` / `subprocess.Popen(…)` resolve the attribute on the same module at call time,\n  so the patch applies without repointing. This covers `test_run_terminus_markup.py`\n  (`psh.subprocess.Popen`, calls `psh.run_terminus` directly — no change), the `psh.time.sleep`\n  lines in `test_terminus_contract.py`/`test_regressions.py`, and every `psh.time.sleep` in the\n  DB suites (`test_db_resilience.py`, `test_traffic_table_rows.py`, `test_db_credentials.py`),\n  whose sleeps are in `db_retry` code that stays in `_legacy` (I5). Leave all of these unchanged —\n  touching them would be unrequested scope.\n\n`tests/README.md:63` documents the seam as `monkeypatch.setattr(psh, \"run_terminus\", fake)`;\nupdate it to the `gateway` seam.\n\n### Diagram — where the wrapper seam lives after I2 (non-local; PD#8)\n\n```\n check/plugin packages ──sc.terminus──►┐\n                                        │\n psh/_legacy.py call sites ─────────────┤ (imported names bound to gateway objects)\n   (B6,B14,B17,B21,B22,B29,B35,B38,B49) │\n                                        ▼\n                         psh/gateway.py: terminus / wp / drush / …\n                                        │  (resolve run_terminus in THIS namespace)\n                                        ▼\n                         psh/gateway.py: run_terminus ──► subprocess.Popen([\"terminus\", …])\n                                        ▲\n                    tests ── monkeypatch.setattr(gateway, \"run_terminus\", fake) ─┘\n```\n\n## New tests (instruments — CAMPAIGN.md §7, PD#14)\n\nThree new assertions. Each names its red demonstration, per the `test_house_rules.py` convention\n(an instrument that cannot be shown to go red is not evidence).\n\n1. **`GatewayResult` return type** (test-first, honest red→green; add to\n   `tests/integration/test_terminus_contract.py`). `run_terminus` and `terminus` each return a\n   `GatewayResult` with `.result`/`.errors`/`.fatal`. RED before the type exists:\n   `psh.GatewayResult` raises `AttributeError`. GREEN after. Scope\n   `(\"check\", \"plugin\", \"dns_classify.py\", \"script_context.py\", \"psh\")`, allowlist\n   `{\"psh/gateway.py\"}`, same nil-guard shape as the existing tests. **RED demonstration\n   (required, then revert):** before the move `subprocess.Popen` lives in `psh/_legacy.py`, so\n   the test (scope includes `psh/`) lists `psh/_legacy.py` as an offender and fails — this is the\n   natural red state the move turns green; the task report pastes it.\n\n3. **Documented `sc` façade names exist** (`tests/unit/test_house_rules.py`). ### ↳ Tool result

```
I have verified the load-bearing claims against the actual code and the two gates. Here is my review.

---

## Adversarial review — I2 Gateway SPEC

**Verification summary of the dispatch's key claims:**
- **(A) Seam decision — CONFIRMED correct.** After the move, `terminus`/`wp`/`drush` resolve `run_terminus` as a global in `psh/gateway.py`'s namespace, so `monkeypatch.setattr(gateway, "run_terminus", …)` is required and `setattr(psh, "run_terminus", …)` would silently call the real subprocess. The four-file / exact-line repoint list is complete and accurate: I grepped every `run_terminus` patch in `tests/` and every enumerated line does patch `run_terminus` and then call a wrapper (`terminus`/`wp`/`drush`/`terminus_data`/`get_old_metrics`→`terminus_data`). The `psh.time.sleep` / `psh.subprocess.Popen` "do-not-repoint" claim is also correct (module-singleton mutation, shared object). No wrapper-driving test is missed; the `sc.terminus`-patching cdn-change tests are façade-level and correctly untouched.
- **(B) CONFIRMED.** The 11 defs match CAMPAIGN §3.1's gateway row exactly; `escape_url` is correctly excluded (§3.1 assigns it to `psh/render.py`, I12).
- **(D) CONFIRMED.** No `_legacy` import is orphaned — `html`(22 uses), `json`, `re`, `time`(1373), `subprocess`(4576), `Any`/`NamedTuple`(139/156), `escape`(50) all retain live users. `sc.terminus = terminus` at line 1643 and `reset_sc.terminus is psh.terminus` stay valid.
- **(G) CONFIRMED.** `ruff-broad.toml` `extend-exclude` names `psh/_legacy.py` (not `psh/`), and `[tool.pyright]` is `include=["psh"]`, `exclude=["psh/_legacy.py"]` — so a new `psh/gateway.py` is gated by both from birth, and nothing needs deleting from `extend-exclude`. The reasoning is sound.

The seam architecture is right. But the **ratchet/verbatim story is broken**, and that is where the real findings are.

---

### Finding 1 — HIGH (Feasibility / Consistency). `run_terminus` trips non-auto-fixable broad-ruff findings the spec never mentions; "verbatim move" and "zero findings" are unsatisfiable together.

The spec claims cleaning is discharged by the tuple-hint replacement:

> "This discharges CAMPAIGN.md §6's house-style-tuple-hint replacement for every moved def in one pass"
> "`psh/gateway.py` MUST pass the broad ruff set and pyright standard with zero findings"

I built a faithful `psh/gateway.py` (real annotations, `GatewayResult` defined, sorted imports) and ran the actual gate. **7 real broad-ruff findings survive** (excluding `N999`, an artifact of my temp filename):

```
2  F541    f-string-missing-placeholders      (the two `short: f"fix WP CLI error"` / `f"fix drush error"`)
1  E713     not-in-test                        (_legacy:375  `not "…read-only Git mode" in line`)
1  PLW2901  redefined-loop-name                (_legacy:370  `line = line.strip()`)
1  C901     run_terminus too complex (12 > 10)   -- NOT auto-fixable
1  PLR0912  too-many-branches (13 > 12)          -- NOT auto-fixable
1  S603     subprocess-without-shell-equals-true -- NOT auto-fixable
```

`C901`, `PLR0912`, and `S603` are **not auto-fixable and not addressable by tuple hints**. To reach "zero findings" the implementer must either (a) **refactor `run_terminus`'s body** — which contradicts the spec's own "bodies unchanged / verbatim move" and endangers the *untested* markup-escaping behavior (`test_run_terminus_markup.py` is the only cover, and CLAUDE.md flags this exact escape logic as shipped-as-a-bug-twice) plus the goldens — or (b) add per-line `# noqa` / grow `ruff-broad.toml`'s ignore list, which CAMPAIGN §13 froze at I0 ("Rules fixed at I0") and would weaken the gate campaign-wide, i.e. a ledger **amendment**.

The spec makes none of this decision. A fresh-context `psh-implementer` hitting `C901` cannot ask — per the Spine, *"implementer subagents have fresh context and cannot ask me. The spec is the only place a seam can be agreed."* This also means acceptance criterion #3 (`uvx ruff check … psh/gateway.py` → "All checks passed!") **cannot pass as written** — PD#14: *"an unrun acceptance suite is PD#14 exactly."*

**Fix:** enumerate all 7 findings in the spec. For the auto-fixable/trivial ones (`F541`×2, `E713`, `PLW2901`) state they are behavior-preserving edits and pin them. For `C901`/`PLR0912`/`S603`, **make an explicit, justified decision** — the low-risk choice is per-line `# noqa: C901,PLR0912` and `# noqa: S603` (with a one-line security rationale for the intentional list-form `subprocess.Popen`), *not* a body refactor (which risks the markup-escape behavior) and *not* an ignore-list change (ratchet drift, needs a §13 amendment + ledger entry). Whichever is chosen, say so in the spec.

---

### Finding 2 — HIGH (Consistency / Testing). "Bodies unchanged; only the return-type annotations change" contradicts the required `GatewayResult` construction, and leaving bare-tuple returns fails the pyright gate.

Two spec sentences collide:

- §Move mechanics: *"holds the eleven defs **verbatim** (bodies unchanged; only the return-type annotations change, below)"*
- §GatewayResult: *"Applied as the return annotation **and constructed at each return** of the 3-tuple wrappers"*

Constructing `GatewayResult(...)` at each `return` **is** a body change. And it is mandatory: I annotated `-> GatewayResult` while leaving the bare-tuple returns (the literal "only the annotations change" reading) and ran the gated pyright — **8 errors**:

```
psh/gateway.py:51:20 - error: Type "tuple[str, str, Literal[True]]" is not assignable to return type "GatewayResult" (reportReturnType)
… (8 total, one per bare-tuple return across run_terminus/terminus/wp/wp_eval/drush/drush_php_script)
8 errors, 0 warnings, 0 informations
```

So the acceptance "0 pyright errors on `psh/gateway.py`" is only reachable by wrapping every return — a body edit the parenthetical denies. Combined with Finding 1's `F541`/`E713`/`PLW2901` edits, the bodies demonstrably change.

This matters beyond pedantry: the column-0-literal handling leans on *"identical nesting, so the interior bytes are unchanged"* (Invariant 8). The implementer needs a **crisp split** between what is byte-preserved (the two column-0 `f"""` literals) and what is edited (return-statement wrapping + the enumerated lint fixes). The current "bodies unchanged" framing muddies exactly that boundary.

**Fix:** reword the §Move mechanics parenthetical to something like *"logic and the two column-0 `f\"\"\"` literals preserved byte-for-byte; return statements wrapped in `GatewayResult(...)`, tuple-hint annotations replaced, and the broad-ruff fixes of Finding 1 applied."*

---

### Finding 3 — MODERATE (Testing / PD#14). The four goldens are **not** a tripwire for the `wp_error`/`drush_error` column-0 literals; the only real safeguard is worded as optional.

The spec's Invariant-8 evidence clause:

> "Evidence required in the task report: the four e2e goldens byte-identical (**they are the tripwire**), plus a token-level **or** diff-of-extracted-literal check on the two blocks."

I checked: **no golden renders either notice.**

```
$ grep -rc 'wp-error\|drush-error\|START WP CLI ERROR\|START DRUSH ERROR' tests/e2e/__snapshots__/*.ambr
… all four files: 0
```

So a re-indentation of the `wp_error`/`drush_error` f-strings leaves all four goldens byte-identical — the goldens **cannot go red** on this change. Worse, the existing shape tests (`test_wp_error_shape`/`test_drush_error_shape`) assert with substring `in` checks (`"<strong>…</strong>" in n["message"]`, `"boom" in n["text"]`) that survive added leading whitespace — they are not a tripwire either. This is precisely the CLAUDE.md gotcha ("`git diff -w` hides it; the goldens are what would actually catch it") **except here the goldens don't catch it**. PD#14: *"A green check is a claim, not evidence, until it has been shown capable of going red on the condition it guards."*

The token/diff-of-extracted-literal check is therefore the **sole** real instrument, yet it is offered as an `or`-branch alternative to a claim that is false.

**Fix:** (1) delete the "they are the tripwire" claim for these two literals and state that no golden renders `wp_error`/`drush_error`; (2) make the extracted-literal byte-equality (or `tokenize`) comparison **mandatory and primary**, and specify it concretely (extract the two `f"""…"""` bodies pre- and post-move, assert byte-identical).

---

### Finding 4 — MODERATE (Testing / PD#14). Instrument #2's RED demonstration is not reproducible at the task it's assigned to.

The no-Popen-outside-gateway test is assigned to **Task 2**, which runs *after* Task 1 has already moved `subprocess.Popen` into `gateway.py`. But its red demo relies on the pre-move state:

> "**RED demonstration (required, then revert):** before the move `subprocess.Popen` lives in `psh/_legacy.py`, so the test … lists `psh/_legacy.py` as an offender and fails — this is the natural red state the move turns green; the task report pastes it."

By Task 2 that "natural red state" no longer exists (the move already turned it green), so the demonstration as described is un-runnable without time travel. Contrast instrument #3, which correctly specifies a *temporary reintroduce-then-revert* ("temporarily removing an `sc.<name>` assignment … then reverted"). PD#14: an instrument that cannot be shown red at implementation time is not evidence.

**Fix:** either (a) move instrument #2's authoring into Task 1 *before* the code move so the natural red is genuine, or (b) keep it in Task 2 but specify a temporary-reintroduction red demo (e.g. add a throwaway `subprocess.Popen(` to a scoped file, observe the failure naming it, revert) — mirroring instrument #3.

---

### Finding 5 — LOW/MODERATE (Completeness / PD#8). A direct `run_terminus` caller in `_legacy` is not routed through a wrapper, so its seam stays `psh.run_terminus` — the "single canonical seam" narrative and diagram omit it.

`psh/_legacy.py:3403` calls `run_terminus(command)` directly (the composer dry-run, B39), not via a wrapper:

```
3402  command = ["composer", live_site, "--", "update", "--dry-run"]
3403  updates, errors, fatal = run_terminus(command)
```

After the import-back this resolves `run_terminus` in `_legacy`'s namespace, so its in-process seam remains `psh.run_terminus` (`_legacy`), **not** `gateway.run_terminus`. The PD#8 diagram lists only wrapper call sites `(B6,B14,…,B49)` flowing into gateway, and the prose says the canonical seam "for anything routed through the wrappers" is `gateway.run_terminus` — technically scoped, but it never notes that a non-wrapper direct caller exists whose seam differs. No test drives 3403 via monkeypatch today (so nothing breaks in I2), but this split is a latent trap for the future author (I8/I9 relocates B39) and a diagram-completeness gap. PD#8: *"a stale diagram is worse than none."*

**Fix:** add one sentence to §Seams noting `_legacy:3403` (composer dry-run) calls `run_terminus` directly, is currently untested via the seam, and keeps `psh.run_terminus` as its patch point until relocated — so no future test patches `gateway.run_terminus` expecting to intercept it.

---

### Finding 6 — LOW (Clarity). `gateway.py`'s own required imports are never enumerated.

The move-mechanics section analyzes only `_legacy`'s *orphans*; it never states what `gateway.py` must import. The moved bodies require `subprocess`, `re`, `json`, `time`, `html`, `from typing import Any, NamedTuple`, `from rich.markup import escape`, and `import script_context as sc`. This is self-correcting via ruff `F821`/pyright/tests, but per the spec bar (*"Could an engineer implement this without asking questions?"*) a one-line import list removes the ambiguity and makes acceptance criterion #3's cleanliness reproducible.

**Fix:** list `gateway.py`'s import block in §Move mechanics.

---

They should be resolved (with the C901/PLR0912/S603 disposition decided in the spec) before an implementer starts, or the first task burns its cycle discovering an unsatisfiable pair of requirements.

59	## Move mechanics
60	
61	### The import-back strategy (keeps the remnant working, one seam for tests)
62	
63	`psh/gateway.py` holds the eleven defs with their **logic and the two column-0 `f"""` notice
64	literals preserved byte-for-byte**; the only edits are (a) return statements wrapped in
65	`GatewayResult(...)`, (b) house-style tuple-hint annotations replaced with real annotations, and
66	(c) the enumerated broad-ruff fixes/suppressions of §Broad-ruff findings. "Verbatim" below means
67	that byte-preserved core, not a literally-unedited file. `psh/_legacy.py` re-imports the defs so
68	its ~54 existing call sites and the `sc`-exposure block keep resolving unchanged:
69	
70	```python
71	# psh/_legacy.py, replacing the removed defs:
72	from psh.gateway import (
73	    GatewayResult,
74	    TerminusError,
75	    drush,

91	import html
92	import json
93	import re
94	import subprocess

96	from typing import Any, NamedTuple
97

99

101	```
102	
103	Consequences, all verified:
104	
105	- `psh._legacy.terminus` / `psh._legacy.run_terminus` / `psh._legacy.TerminusError` /
106	  `psh._legacy.GatewayResult` etc. still exist (bound to the gateway objects), so `psh.<name>`
107	  through the test `psh` fixture keeps resolving. `sc.terminus = terminus` (`_legacy` line 1643)
108	  still assigns the gateway function, so `reset_sc.terminus is psh.terminus` stays true
109	  (`test_terminus_contract.py::test_check_helpers_are_exposed_on_sc`).
110	- **No `_legacy` imports are orphaned by the move.** Every import the moved code used has other
111	  live users in `_legacy`: `html` (plugin/module notice bodies, ~9 sites), `time` (`time.sleep`
112	  at db-retry line 1373), `escape` (50 call sites), `Any` (`process_config`), `subprocess`
113	  (PHP inliner), `json`/`re`/`NamedTuple`. Verified by grep; the implementer re-verifies and
114	  removes only what its change actually orphans (there should be none).
115	
116	### `GatewayResult` (CAMPAIGN.md §6)
117	
118	```python
119	class GatewayResult(NamedTuple):
120	    result: Any
121	    errors: str
122	    fatal: bool
123	```
124	
125	Applied as the return annotation and constructed at each return of the 3-tuple wrappers:
126	`run_terminus`, `terminus`, `wp`, `wp_eval`, `drush`, `drush_php_script`. `fix_drush_output`
127	keeps its 2-tuple, annotated `-> tuple[str, str]`. `terminus_data` returns just the result,
128	annotated `-> Any`. `wp_error`/`drush_error` return `-> list[dict[str, str]]`. This discharges
129	CAMPAIGN.md §6's house-style-tuple-hint replacement for every moved def in one pass (D2 — cleaned
130	as it moves, never fixed in place in the remnant).
131	
132	`GatewayResult` is a `tuple` subclass, so every positional unpack (`result, errors, fatal = …`)
133	and every `== (a, b, c)` comparison in call sites and tests is unchanged — behavior-preserving,
134	no golden impact (the return type is invisible to rendered output). The first element of
135	`run_terminus`/`wp_eval` is textual output; the generic field name `result` covers it and no
136	caller reads the fields by name, so this is a naming nicety only.
137	
138	`GatewayResult` is **not** added to `sc`: no `check`/`plugin` consumer references the type name
139	(they unpack positionally), so adding it would be dead façade surface (CAMPAIGN.md §17 Q4).
140	
141	### Broad-ruff findings on the moved code (decided here, not left to the implementer)
142	
143	Under `ruff-broad.toml` (`select = ["ALL"]`), the moved code trips seven findings beyond the
144	tuple-hint replacement. They are enumerated with a **decided** disposition so a fresh-context
145	implementer never has to choose (CAMPAIGN.md §Spec quality bar: the spec is the only place a
146	decision can be agreed). None of these dispositions changes `ruff-broad.toml`'s frozen ignore
147	list (that would be a §13 amendment) — all are inline, per-line `# noqa` or behavior-preserving
148	edits.
149	
150	| Rule | Where | Disposition |
151	|---|---|---|
152	| `F541` ×2 | `wp_error`/`drush_error` `"short": f"fix WP CLI error"` / `f"fix drush error"` | **Fix**: drop the `f` prefix. Placeholder-less f-string → identical `str`; not in a fragile path. |
153	| `E713` | `run_terminus` stderr-filter loop (`not "…read-only Git mode" in line`) | **Fix**: `"…read-only Git mode" not in line`. One-operator swap, provably identical, outside the escaping/exit-code logic. |
154	| `PLW2901` | `run_terminus` same loop (`line = line.strip()` shadows the loop var) | **Fix**: iterate `for raw_line in lines: line = raw_line.strip()` (keep `line` as the working name so the conditions/append are unchanged). Behavior-preserving. |
155	| `C901` | `run_terminus` (complexity 12 > 10) | **`# noqa: C901`** on the `def`. "Fixing" it means restructuring `run_terminus`, whose stderr/markup escaping is under-tested (only `test_run_terminus_markup.py` + the goldens cover it, and CLAUDE.md records it shipped as a bug twice). Refactoring is a review activity, not part of a behavior-preserving move (`prompts/implementation-standards.md` § Test discipline). |
156	| `PLR0912` | `run_terminus` (branches 13 > 12) | **`# noqa: PLR0912`** on the `def`, same rationale as `C901`. |
157	| `S603` | `run_terminus` `subprocess.Popen(command, …)` | **`# noqa: S603`** with an inline reason: `command` is a fixed `["terminus", …]` argv (no shell, no untrusted-input execution path); the spawn is the gateway's entire purpose. |
158	
159	So `run_terminus`'s **body logic** is moved unchanged except the two cosmetic loop fixes (`E713`,
160	`PLW2901`), which touch only the benign-warning stderr filter — not the escaping, the returncode
161	handling, or the `wp`/`composer` output filter. The three suppressions carry inline reasons (a
162	bare `# noqa` is itself a silent failure — PD#1 / `prompts/implementation-standards.md` §1). With
163	these applied, acceptance criterion #3 (`ruff check --config ruff-broad.toml psh/gateway.py` →
164	"All checks passed!", pyright 0 errors) is reachable; the implementer MUST paste it.
165	
166	### Column-0 literal invariant (Invariant 8)
167	
168	`wp_error` and `drush_error` each contain a multi-line `f"""..."""` whose continuation lines
169	begin at **column 0**. They are module-level defs today and stay module-level defs in
170	`gateway.py` — identical nesting, so the interior bytes must be unchanged. The implementer MUST
171	move these literals **verbatim** and MUST NOT re-indent them; `git diff -w` is not acceptable
172	evidence (CAMPAIGN.md Invariant 8).
173	
174	**The goldens are NOT a tripwire here.** No golden renders either notice — `wp_error`/`drush_error`
175	fire only on a WP/Drush *command failure*, which the offline fixtures never produce
176	(`grep -rc 'START WP CLI ERROR\|START DRUSH ERROR' tests/e2e/__snapshots__/*.ambr` → all zero).
177	The existing `test_wp_error_shape`/`test_drush_error_shape` assert with substring `in`, which
178	survives added leading whitespace, so they are not a tripwire either. The **sole** real
179	instrument is therefore mandatory and primary: extract the two `f"""…"""` bodies from the pre-move
180	source (`git show <I1-closing-sha>:psh/_legacy.py`) and from `psh/gateway.py`, and assert them
181	**byte-identical** (a `diff` of the extracted blocks is empty). The task report pastes that diff.
182	
183	## Seams (declared before implementation — CAMPAIGN.md §Spec quality bar)
184	
185	The canonical in-process seam for anything routed through the wrappers becomes
186	**`psh.gateway.run_terminus`**. Reason: after the move, `terminus`/`wp`/`drush` resolve
187	`run_terminus` in the **gateway** module's namespace, not `_legacy`'s. Patching
188	`psh._legacy.run_terminus` (i.e. `setattr(psh, "run_terminus", …)`) would rebind only the
189	remnant's name and the wrappers would call the real subprocess — a silent test defect (PD#14).
190	
191	A conftest fixture provides the handle:
192	
193	```python
194	@pytest.fixture
195	def gateway(psh):
196	    """The psh.gateway module (psh._legacy has already imported it)."""
197	    import psh.gateway
198	    return psh.gateway
199	```
200	
201	**What must repoint (function-attribute patches):** only the four files whose tests patch
202	`run_terminus` **and then call a wrapper** — the patch target changes from `psh` to `gateway`:
203	
204	| File | Lines patching `run_terminus` |
205	|---|---|
206	| `tests/integration/test_terminus_contract.py` | 21, 29, 38, 44, 49, 57, 67, 82 |
207	| `tests/integration/test_wrappers.py` | 23, 31, 38, 46, 54, 62 |
208	| `tests/integration/test_terminus_seam.py` | 15, 26 |
209	| `tests/integration/test_regressions.py` | 31, 48 |
210	
211	**What must NOT repoint (module-singleton patches — verified they keep working):**
212	
213	- `setattr(psh.time, "sleep", …)` and `setattr(psh.subprocess, "Popen", …)` mutate the shared
214	  `time` / `subprocess` **module** objects, which gateway and `_legacy` both `import`. Gateway's
215	  `time.sleep(5)` / `subprocess.Popen(…)` resolve the attribute on the same module at call time,
216	  so the patch applies without repointing. This covers `test_run_terminus_markup.py`
217	  (`psh.subprocess.Popen`, calls `psh.run_terminus` directly — no change), the `psh.time.sleep`
218	  lines in `test_terminus_contract.py`/`test_regressions.py`, and every `psh.time.sleep` in the
219	  DB suites (`test_db_resilience.py`, `test_traffic_table_rows.py`, `test_db_credentials.py`),
220	  whose sleeps are in `db_retry` code that stays in `_legacy` (I5). Leave all of these unchanged —
221	  touching them would be unrequested scope.
222	
223	`tests/README.md:63` documents the seam as `monkeypatch.setattr(psh, "run_terminus", fake)`;
224	update it to the `gateway` seam.
225	
226	**One non-wrapper direct caller keeps a different seam (latent-trap note for later increments).**
227	`psh/_legacy.py:3403` (the Drupal composer dry-run, B35/B39) calls `run_terminus(command)`
228	directly, not through a wrapper. After the import-back, that name resolves to `_legacy`'s imported
229	binding, so its in-process patch point stays `psh.run_terminus` (i.e. `setattr(psh, …)`), **not**
230	`gateway.run_terminus` — patching the gateway binding would not intercept it (separate name
231	bindings to the same function object). No current test drives line 3403 via monkeypatch (it is
232	exercised only by the e2e PATH-shim `terminus`), so nothing breaks in I2; this is a note so the
233	author who relocates B39 (I8/I9) does not assume the gateway seam reaches it. It is shown as the
234	dashed edge in the diagram below.
235	
236	### Diagram — where the wrapper seam lives after I2 (non-local; PD#8)
237	
238	```
239	 check/plugin packages ──sc.terminus──►┐
240	                                        │
241	 psh/_legacy.py wrapper call sites ─────┤ (imported names bound to gateway objects)
242	   (B6,B14,B17,B21,B22,B29,B35,B38,B49) │
243	                                        ▼
244	                         psh/gateway.py: terminus / wp / drush / …
245	                                        │  (resolve run_terminus in THIS namespace)
246	                                        ▼
247	                         psh/gateway.py: run_terminus ──► subprocess.Popen(["terminus", …])
248	                                        ▲
249	                    tests ── monkeypatch.setattr(gateway, "run_terminus", fake) ─┘
250	
251	 psh/_legacy.py:3403 (composer dry-run) ┈┈► run_terminus  [resolves _legacy's binding;
252	                                             seam stays psh.run_terminus until B39 relocates]
253	```
254	
255	## New tests (instruments — CAMPAIGN.md §7, PD#14)
256	
257	Three new assertions. Each names its red demonstration, per the `test_house_rules.py` convention
258	(an instrument that cannot be shown to go red is not evidence).
259	
260	1. **`GatewayResult` return type** (test-first, honest red→green; add to
261	   `tests/integration/test_terminus_contract.py`). `run_terminus` and `terminus` each return a
262	   `GatewayResult` with `.result`/`.errors`/`.fatal`. RED before the type exists:
263	   `psh.GatewayResult` raises `AttributeError`. GREEN after. Uses the `gateway` seam for the
264	   `terminus` case; a `subprocess.Popen` fake for the `run_terminus` case (mirroring
265	   `test_run_terminus_markup.py`).
266	
267	2. **No subprocess spawn outside the gateway** (`tests/unit/test_house_rules.py`). Among feature
268	   code, `subprocess.Popen(` appears only in `psh/gateway.py`. Mechanizes CLAUDE.md's
269	   "Never shell out to terminus/wp/drush directly": `run_terminus` is the only terminus spawner
270	   and `subprocess.Popen` is how it spawns; the PHP inliner uses `subprocess.run` and is not a
271	   terminus/wp/drush call, so it is correctly not matched. Scope
272	   `("check", "plugin", "dns_classify.py", "script_context.py", "psh")`, allowlist
273	   `{"psh/gateway.py"}`, same nil-guard shape as the existing tests. **RED demonstration
274	   (required, then revert):** this test is authored in Task 2, *after* Task 1 has already moved
275	   `subprocess.Popen` into `gateway.py`, so the pre-move natural-red state no longer exists at
276	   authoring time. Demonstrate red the way instrument #3 does — by *temporary reintroduction*:
277	   add a throwaway `subprocess.Popen(` line to a scoped file (e.g. `script_context.py`), observe
278	   the test fail naming that file, then revert. The task report pastes that red output.
279	   (Alternatively the implementer MAY author this test at the very start of Task 1, before
280	   creating `gateway.py`, and capture the genuine pre-move red listing `psh/_legacy.py`; either
281	   is acceptable, but silence is not — PD#14.)
282	
283	3. **Documented `sc` façade names exist** (`tests/unit/test_house_rules.py`). Pins CAMPAIGN.md
284	   Invariant 9 / §3.5 ("sc names never removed mid-campaign"). Asserts every name in CLAUDE.md's
285	   runtime-exposed block is present on the loaded `sc`:
286	   `("escape_url", "check_wordpress_plugin", "check_drupal_module", "umich_enabled",
287	   "cloudflare_enabled", "terminus", "fqdn_re", "db_engine_args")`. This is a **pinning**
288	   test (it passes when written, like the two existing house rules); its red state is
289	   demonstrated by temporarily removing an `sc.<name>` assignment and observed in the docstring,
290	   then reverted — the carve-out the existing house-rules file already documents for itself.
291	
292	## Ratchet (CAMPAIGN.md §13)
293	
294	`psh/gateway.py` is a **new** file and therefore **not** in `ruff-broad.toml`'s `extend-exclude`
295	(only `psh/_legacy.py` and the other named remnants are). It is gated by the broad ruff set and
296	pyright standard mode (`[tool.pyright]` `include = ["psh"]`, `exclude = ["psh/_legacy.py"]`) from
297	birth. Nothing is deleted from `extend-exclude` this increment — the "un-grandfather the wrapper
298	functions" note in LEDGER.md I0 assumed the functions would stay in an excluded file; because
299	they move to a fresh file the exclude list is untouched and the cleaning obligation is discharged
300	by gateway.py being born under the full gate. `psh/gateway.py` MUST pass the broad ruff set and
301	pyright standard with zero findings (§7 obligation 3, D2). Record this reasoning in the ledger.

### The concern (SPEC deviation — reported per "no silent deviation")

The SPEC §Broad-ruff table enumerated "seven findings beyond the tuple-hint replacement" and requires `gateway.py` to pass with **zero** findings — but it did not anticipate that wrapping `run_terminus`'s three **literal-boolean** returns in the `GatewayResult(...)` *constructor* trips **FBT003** (`Boolean positional value in function call`). A bare tuple literal `(output, errors, True)` is not a call, so FBT003 did not exist pre-move; the wrapping introduced it. The other wrappers pass `fatal` as a *variable*, so only `run_terminus` is affected.

I resolved it behavior-preservingly with keyword arguments (`GatewayResult(output, errors, fatal=True/False)`) — the canonical FBT003 fix. This touches neither `ruff-broad.toml`'s ignore list nor adds a `noqa`, and matches the SPEC's own stated preference for behavior-preserving fixes over suppressions. It does not affect the goldens or any test. Flagging it so the reviewer/controller knows the SPEC's finding enumeration was incomplete and can confirm the disposition.

I read the Spine (`prompts/directives.md`), `prompts/adversarial-review.md`, the CLAUDE.md architecture/testing sections, and the I2 SPEC in full, then verified every load-bearing claim by running commands rather than trusting the diff or any report.

## Verdict: **APPROVED**

Nothing survived scrutiny as a defect. All eight review axes pass. Two non-blocking observations are recorded at the end so the ledger/task-report stays honest (PD#14/PD#9), but neither requires a code change.

## Evidence by axis

**A. Behavior preservation / goldens — PASS.** `git diff 8b1466b 7044b12 -- tests/e2e/__snapshots__/` is empty (four goldens byte-identical). `./run-tests --fast --llm` is green on all three gates: `LLM_SUMMARY passed=751 failed=0 error=0 skipped=1`, `27 snapshots passed`. ```
wp msg / wp txt / dr msg / dr txt : byte-identical=True (all four)
```
The only per-function edits are the sanctioned ones: return annotation `-> list[dict]` → `-> list[dict[str, str]]` and the F541 `f"fix WP CLI error"`/`f"fix drush error"` → non-f-string. The interior column-0 continuation lines are untouched. No golden renders these notices (they fire only on WP/Drush command failure), so this extraction is the real instrument, and it is clean.

**C. The seam — PASS, and I proved it can go red.** I ran an in-process check: patching `gateway.run_terminus` intercepts `legacy.terminus(...)` (returns the fake `GatewayResult({}, '', False)`); patching only the `_legacy` binding does **not** — the wrapper resolved gateway's real `run_terminus` and returned `REAL_SUBPROCESS`. So the repoint from `psh`→`gateway` was mandatory and the green is meaningful (a mispointed patch would call through and fail). All eight patch-and-call-wrapper sites in the four files (`test_terminus_contract`, `test_wrappers`, `test_terminus_seam`, `test_regressions`) target `gateway.run_terminus` and each such test function declares the `gateway` fixture. `grep` confirms **zero** remaining `setattr(psh, "run_terminus", …)` in the tree, so no wrapper test silently calls through. Every `psh.time.sleep` / `psh.subprocess.Popen` patch (including the direct-call `test_run_terminus_markup.py` and `test_terminus_contract.py:37,119`) correctly stayed on `psh` — `git diff` shows none of them changed. These work because `_legacy` and `gateway` share the same `time`/`subprocess` module objects; confirmed by the passing retry tests.

**D. GatewayResult correctness — PASS.** It is a `NamedTuple` (tuple subclass), so positional unpack, `== (a,b,c)`, and indexing are behavior-preserving; goldens byte-identical confirms invisibility to output. `terminus_data` returns bare `Any` (line 173, `return result`); `fix_drush_output` returns `tuple[str, str]` (line 241). The `fatal=True`/`fatal=False` keyword usage is correct and consistent — the three literal-bool constructions (lines 63, 116, 118) use the keyword; the variable-`fatal` constructions (170, 201, 212, 277, 294) do not need it.

**E. Import-back & orphans — PASS.** `_legacy` re-imports all 12 names (lines 306–319) matching the SPEC list; `sc.terminus = terminus` still assigns the gateway function (line 1367). No import is orphaned: `html`(20), `json`(7), `re`(8), `subprocess`(1, the PHP inliner at line 4300), `time`(42), `Any`(4), `NamedTuple`(3, `TrafficRow`/`OverageProtectionRow`), `escape`(20) all retain live users. `escape_url` correctly stayed in `_legacy` (line 302, I12 scope).

**F. Ruff/pyright — PASS.** `uvx ruff check --config ruff-broad.toml psh/gateway.py` → "All checks passed!". Pyright (run in the project venv as `run-tests` does) → `0 errors`. Note the standalone `uvx pyright` reports a spurious `rich.markup` import error because its isolated env lacks project deps — not a real finding; `run-tests` runs pyright inside the venv where it is clean. All three noqas carry inline reasons (C901/PLR0912 on the `run_terminus` def line 31; S603 on the Popen line 44); no bare noqa (PD#1). No over-suppression — I confirmed each is a real finding: removing the S603 argv is the gateway's purpose, and the C901/PLR0912 rationale (under-tested escaping, refactor is review work) matches `prompts/implementation-standards.md`.

**G. The GatewayResult test — PASS, genuine red.** `test_run_terminus_returns_gatewayresult` and `test_terminus_returns_gatewayresult` both assert `isinstance(res, psh.GatewayResult)`. Before the type existed, `psh.GatewayResult` raises `AttributeError` (red); and if a wrapper returned a plain tuple, `isinstance` is `False` (red). Not a tautology. The run_terminus case uses a `subprocess.Popen` fake; the terminus case uses the `gateway` seam — exactly as SPEC §"New tests" item 1 specifies.

**H. Scope discipline — PASS.** The `_legacy` diff is a single hunk (`@@ -303,296 +303,20 @@`): the 11 defs removed, replaced only by the import block (verified — no added line outside the import block). `ruff-broad.toml` and `pyproject.toml` are untouched (the exclude/ignore lists are unchanged, as the SPEC §Ratchet requires — gateway.py is born under the full gate). `test_house_rules.py` is correctly **not** in this commit (the no-Popen and sc-façade tests are Task 2). The PHP-inliner `subprocess.run` (line 4300) was left in place.

## Non-blocking observations (record, don't fix)

1. **SPEC undercounted broad-ruff findings as "seven."** Wrapping returns in `GatewayResult(output, errors, True)` introduces an **8th** finding — FBT003 (Boolean positional value) — which the SPEC's §"Broad-ruff findings" table does not enumerate. I confirmed it fires: substituting positional `True`/`False` back in yields `FBT003` at lines 63/116/118. The implementer resolved it correctly and cleanly with the `fatal=` keyword (also more readable), so the gate is genuinely at zero findings. This is a SPEC-accuracy gap, not an implementation defect; worth a one-line note in the Task 1 report / ledger so the "seven findings" claim isn't propagated. The dispatch's own item D already anticipated this fix and it is correct.

2. **Wrapper docstrings still say "Returns a 3-tuple."** `wp`/`wp_eval`/`drush`/`drush_php_script` (lines 192, 208, 267, 284) describe the return as a "3-tuple" rather than a `GatewayResult`. This is not wrong (a `GatewayResult` *is* a 3-field tuple subclass) and the SPEC did not require docstring updates, but a later reader looking for the typed return may want the name. Trivial; optional for Task 3's doc pass.

## Spine directives applied (by number, verbatim clauses)

- **PD#14** — *"A green check is a claim, not evidence, until it has been shown capable of going red on the condition it guards."* Both instruments pass when written, so I demonstrated each going red on the exact condition it guards (a scoped `subprocess.Popen`; a removed `sc` name) before trusting green.
- **PD#1 (Zero silent failures)** — *"A failure that can happen silently is a critical defect."* Both invariants guard silent failures — a raw shell-out bypassing the wrapper, and a dropped `sc` façade name that breaks standalone check-module tests without any other alarm.
- **PD#3 (Data flows have shadow paths)** — *"nil input, empty/zero-length input, and upstream error."* The nil-guard (`len(sources) > 20`) covers the empty-glob shadow so a moved/renamed directory fails loudly instead of passing vacuously.
- **Engineering Preferences (DRY)** — *"flag repetition aggressively."* Rather than duplicate the dir/file globbing, I parameterized the existing `_scoped_sources` helper by scope and updated its one prior caller.

38	def _scoped_sources(scope):
39	    """Every feature-code source file under `scope`, resolved relative to the repo root."""
40	    files = []
41	    for entry in scope:
42	        path = REPO / entry
43	        if path.is_dir():
44	            files.extend(sorted(path.rglob("*.py")))
45	        elif path.is_file():
46	            files.append(path)
47	    return files
48	
49	
50	def test_only_two_files_read_os_environ_directly():
51	    """CLAUDE.md's os.environ invariant, pinned.
52	
53	    RED DEMONSTRATION (PD#14, observed 2026-07-16): adding `os.environ` to a third file in
54	    scope -- e.g. check/dns/hook.py -- fails this test naming that file.  Verified, then
55	    reverted.  A green run here is only evidence because that red run happened.
56	    """
57	    sources = _scoped_sources(ENVIRON_SCOPE)
58	    # Nil guard: an empty glob would make every assertion below vacuously true -- GREEN,
59	    # having checked nothing.  That is the e2e-goldens-never-loaded-checks defect in
60	    # miniature (PD#14), so a moved/renamed directory MUST fail loudly here.

62	        f"scope resolved to {len(sources)} files -- a directory in ENVIRON_SCOPE moved or "
63	        f"was renamed.  Fix the scope; do not weaken this test."
64	    )

## Findings

### 1. (Low / non-blocking, pre-existing) The `os.environ` house-rule is blind to the entire program body `psh/`

`tests/unit/test_house_rules.py:27` still scopes the PD#6 guard to the 638-byte shim:

```python
ENVIRON_SCOPE = ("check", "plugin", "dns_classify.py", "script_context.py",
                 "pantheon-sitehealth-emails")   # ← the shim, not psh/
```

while its sibling added this increment gets it right (`POPEN_SCOPE = (..., "psh")`, line 107). I confirmed the divergence:

```
psh in ENVIRON_SCOPE: False
psh in POPEN_SCOPE:  True
```

`ENVIRON_SCOPE`'s `"pantheon-sitehealth-emails"` resolves to the ~17-line shim (`-rwxr-xr-x ... 638 ... pantheon-sitehealth-emails`), so a direct `os.environ` read added to `psh/_legacy.py` or `psh/gateway.py` — the largest feature-code files in the repo — passes this test **silently**. It is latent today (`grep -rn os.environ psh/` → none), and it predates I2 (it dates to I0 when the body moved into `psh/`), so it is not a defect *introduced* by these three tasks. But this is exactly the instrument the dispatch asked me to scrutinize, PD#6's mechanical half now fails to cover the program body, and I2 is the increment that (a) parameterized `_scoped_sources` making the fix a one-word addition and (b) placed the correct `psh`-inclusive scope one constant away.

- **Evidence it's a real gap, not intended:** the docstring/comment cites CLAUDE.md's "Credentials are never read from the environment by **feature code**" — and `psh/_legacy.py` is feature code.
- **Fix:** add `"psh"` to `ENVIRON_SCOPE` (drop the now-redundant `"pantheon-sitehealth-emails"` shim entry, or keep it). Allowlist stays correct (`psh/` has no `os.environ`), nil-guard stays satisfied, suite stays green. The uncommitted `development/2026-07-17-mod-I2-gateway/` folder + the closing commit are the natural home; if deferred, it should be written down as an open question in the LEDGER (PD#9) rather than left silent.

Relevant paths: `/workspace/tests/unit/test_house_rules.py`, `/workspace/psh/gateway.py`, `/workspace/psh/_legacy.py`, `/workspace/CLAUDE.md`, `/workspace/development/2026-07-17-modularization-campaign/LEDGER.md`.

name: archive-session
description: Archive the current Claude session into development/<date-slug>/ (transcript, statistics, analytics scaffold) at the end of a feature, before committing. User-invoked only — type /archive-session.

# Archiving a development session

Run this at the end of a feature-development session, after the work is done but
**before committing**. It populates the feature's `development/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug>/`
folder with the record artifacts, then hands back to the user to commit.

Do the deterministic, secret-sensitive work (rendering, scrubbing, token math) via
`development/finalize-session.py` — never eyeball-redact a transcript yourself. This
skill's job is only to (a) figure out the target folder, (b) capture the two things
the script can't reach from outside a live session, and (c) run the script.

## Steps

1. **Determine the target folder.** It is `development/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug>/` for the
   feature just built. If the user passed a slug as the argument, use
   `development/<that>/`. Otherwise infer it from the active `SPEC.md`, the git branch,
   or the feature under discussion; if it's ambiguous, ask the user. Create the folder
   if it doesn't exist. If prompts weren't saved yet, remind the user that
   `NN-*.prompt.md` files and any `design-notes/` are part of the record.

2. **Capture in-session-only data to a gitignored `*.raw.txt` file** in the folder:
   - **/usage (dollar cost)** — you **cannot** invoke `/usage` yourself (it's a
     built-in CLI command, not a tool). Ask the user to run `/usage` and paste its
     output, then save that verbatim to `<dir>/usage.raw.txt`. This is the source of
     the cost figure — the script has no price table. If the user skips it, proceed;
     the cost section will just say it wasn't captured.

   The `.raw.txt` file is gitignored; the script folds its contents into
   `statistics.md`.

3. **Run the script.** From the repo root:
   ```
   python development/finalize-session.py --dir development/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug> \
       [--usage-capture development/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug>/usage.raw.txt] \
       [--label NN]
   ```
   It defaults to the newest session JSONL under `~/.claude/projects/-workspace/`.
   Pass `--label NN` only for a feature spanning multiple sessions (produces
   `transcript-NN.md` / `statistics-NN.md`). Omit `--usage-capture` if you didn't create it.
   This writes `transcript.md` (scrubbed, committed), `transcript.raw.md` (gitignored),
   and `statistics.md` (committed).

4. **Scaffold `analytics.md`** in the folder if it doesn't already exist — a short
   template for the user's own narrative analysis (distinct from the auto-generated
   `statistics.md`, which is machine-written; do not hand-edit `statistics.md`):
   ```markdown
   # Analytics — <feature>

   _Your narrative: what went well, what to do differently, decisions worth remembering._
   ```

5. **Verify and report — do NOT commit.** Confirm `transcript.md` scrubbed cleanly
   with a **value-shaped** grep (matches actual secret VALUES, not prose mentions of
```

So the transcript archiving is genuinely your step. I'll make the closing docs commit now (all the substantive work), leaving only the auto-generated archive artifacts for you.

## Assistant

**Increment I2 (gateway extraction) is complete and landed on `main`.** Working tree clean, four e2e goldens byte-identical, memory recorded.

## What I2 did

Extracted the eleven Terminus/WP/Drush subprocess wrappers (`run_terminus`, `terminus`, `terminus_data`, `wp`, `wp_eval`, `wp_error`, `drush`, `drush_php_script`, `drush_error`, `fix_drush_output`, `TerminusError`) out of the 4,700-line remnant into a new `psh/gateway.py` — the campaign's future Pantheon-API transport seam (CAMPAIGN.md D1). Introduced the `GatewayResult` NamedTuple as the typed return. `psh/_legacy.py` re-imports them so its ~54 call sites and the `sc` façade resolve unchanged.

## Process followed (per CAMPAIGN.md §12)

Read the governing docs → wrote SPEC.md → **adversarial spec review** (caught two unsatisfiable "verbatim + zero-findings" contradictions before any code was written) → three subagent-driven tasks (`psh-implementer`), each reviewed → **whole-branch review**.

## The load-bearing decision

The monkeypatch seam moved from `psh.run_terminus` to **`psh.gateway.run_terminus`** (wrappers now resolve `run_terminus` in the gateway namespace). Four test files were repointed via a new `gateway` fixture. Module-singleton patches (`psh.time.sleep`, `psh.subprocess.Popen`) correctly needed no change. The reviewer independently proved the seam can go red.

## Commits (on `main`, baseline `8b1466b`)

- `7044b12` — gateway move + `GatewayResult` + seam repoint
- `0141f76` — two house-rule instruments (gateway-only-subprocess, sc-façade-names)
- `cf661d2` — **review finding**: the `os.environ` PD#6 house rule was blind to the whole `psh/` program body; widened its scope and proved the new red state
- `fe3d5a8` — closing docs (CLAUDE.md, README, ledger, dev folder)

Full suite at close (live tier present): **755 passed / 1 skipped**, all three gates green, 27 snapshots. One spec deviation, cleanly resolved and ledgered: the `GatewayResult(...)` constructor introduced an eighth ruff finding (FBT003) the spec undercounted as seven — fixed with `fatal=` keyword args, no ratchet change.

The transcript archive — `/archive-session` is user-invocation-only and its cost figure needs you to run `/usage`. Everything else is done. Next up is **I3** (`psh/configuration.py` + the `Notice` class), per the ledger.

   ```
   This should return nothing; any hit is a real secret value that slipped the regex —
   surface it, don't commit. (A bare quoted word that happens to look like a token is
   left alone by design.) List what was written. Then tell the user the folder is ready
   and that they can ask you to commit everything (code + `development/<dir>/`) in one
   commit, with you writing the commit message.
